  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cf053daf-be39-44eb-893c-1a09f5cd9dd3'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15642307777287193163">The Chronicles of Neffie is the first of six novel series centered around Neffie, a fifteen year old slave girl growing up in the Deep South. Loosely based on true life events, Neffie takes readers on a tumultuous journey as she navigates her day to day life as a slave in Colbert County, Alabama. Told from the perspective of a fifteen year old slave girl, Neffie’s experien</span>
  <span id="freeText15642307777287193163" style="display:none">The Chronicles of Neffie is the first of six novel series centered around Neffie, a fifteen year old slave girl growing up in the Deep South. Loosely based on true life events, Neffie takes readers on a tumultuous journey as she navigates her day to day life as a slave in Colbert County, Alabama. Told from the perspective of a fifteen year old slave girl, Neffie’s experiences are heart wrenching and riveting.<br /><br /><br />The Chronicles of Neffie is a harrowing account full of twists and turns that will have readers anxiously waiting to see what will happen next. What will come of Neffie? Only time will tell. This is only the beginning. Let the journey begin.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10468295394099137940"><strong>Astounding portrayal of a young slave.</strong><br/><br/>I have chosen a fove star rating because this book to riveted me to every page. Well written and executed in a manner consistent with the modern black view on slavery on the south. Isply loved this book and want more about Neffies life. </span>

<div id="review_2301375711" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2301375711" />
    <a title="Kim Walton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56683148-kim-walton"><img alt="Kim Walton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520541508p2/56683148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2301375711?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim Walton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim Walton" href="/user/show/56683148-kim-walton">Kim Walton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38331186-the-chronicles-of-neffie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56683148-kim-walton?shelf=afro-american-history">afro-american-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56683148-kim-walton?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56683148-kim-walton?shelf=urban-fiction">urban-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56683148-kim-walton?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2301375711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11910323409550990002"><strong>History, not a bad start at all.</strong><br/><br/>Neffie's, story is getting interesting. reading the story from the view point of a slave child, actually made me feel even more compassion for what they went through. I can't imagine what it was like for someone to be degraded in all types of ways, without snapping. I felt for those young girls, men, and women. To be treated like an animal and less than human. <br/>Slavery is one of those topics that people don't want to talk about, much less read about. But it is hist</span>
  <span id="freeText11910323409550990002" style="display:none"><strong>History, not a bad start at all.</strong><br /><br />Neffie's, story is getting interesting. reading the story from the view point of a slave child, actually made me feel even more compassion for what they went through. I can't imagine what it was like for someone to be degraded in all types of ways, without snapping. I felt for those young girls, men, and women. To be treated like an animal and less than human. <br />Slavery is one of those topics that people don't want to talk about, much less read about. But it is history,and like all other stories should be told. This book is one that I would recommend to schools. Have the students read and discuss it. Discuss the break down of the Afro-American family and the systematic division that was deliberately done. I would read part two to see what Neffie, has to do to save herself, and her family.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11910323409550990002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2335116755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2335116755" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2335116755?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2335116755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5378698837646549825">‘Do you still think that life here in the Deep South is grand? If you’re a slave, it sure ain’t. If you’re White, maybe so.’<br/><br/>Author A.L. (Anita) Gibson has published five books to date, POKA CITY BLUES was her well-received debut. Now she is writing a series - THE CHRONICLES OF NEFFIE – of which this is book 1. In addition to novels she also writes short stories and poetry.<br/><br/>We know from the synopsis the overall flow of this series set in 1837 – ‘The Chronicles of Neffie is the first of six novel s</span>
  <span id="freeText5378698837646549825" style="display:none">‘Do you still think that life here in the Deep South is grand? If you’re a slave, it sure ain’t. If you’re White, maybe so.’<br /><br />Author A.L. (Anita) Gibson has published five books to date, POKA CITY BLUES was her well-received debut. Now she is writing a series - THE CHRONICLES OF NEFFIE – of which this is book 1. In addition to novels she also writes short stories and poetry.<br /><br />We know from the synopsis the overall flow of this series set in 1837 – ‘The Chronicles of Neffie is the first of six novel series centered around Neffie, a fifteen year old slave girl growing up in the Deep South. Loosely based on true life events, Neffie takes readers on a tumultuous journey as she navigates her day to day life as a slave in Colbert County, Alabama. Told from the perspective of a fifteen-year-old slave girl, Neffie’s experiences are heart wrenching and compelling. What will come of Neffie? Only time will tell. This is only the beginning. Let the journey begin.’<br /><br />From this overview we are introduced to the atmosphere of The South in a well-formed Prologue to this initial volume – ‘The South. Some folks say it’s the greatest place on earth. Other folks say it’s a tough place to be. To be free that is. I’ve heard plenty of folks say that the South is on the rise again because of all the Southern hospitality and that good ole Southern charm. I guess that all depends on who you ask. I myself wouldn’t know anything about all that because my life here in the South is much different. You see, I was born in eighteen thirty seven as a slave in Colbert County, Alabama, so my life here in the South ain’t all that great. For you folks that ain’t familiar with Colbert County, Alabama, it’s a part of the Muscle Shoals and Florence area and it’s not too far off from the Tennessee River. There’s a lotta land to be had out here, but there’s more fields and water than anything else. Manors and plantations are just about everywhere and they’re filled to the brim with slaves. Massa Piero Sanderson is the man who owns me, my Mama, my Papa and my three older brothers. Together we all live in one of the many slave cabins on Massa Sanderson’s sprawling Oak Manor. Neffie is the name that was given to me by my Mama because that was the only name she could think of at the time when she gave birth to me. Massa Sanderson likes to call me sumthin’ else. Ragazza Nera is what he sometimes calls me which means Black Girl in Italian and I can’t stand it. No, I absolutely hate it. For the life of me, I can’t understand why this man hardly calls me by my name. Sometimes I think he does it on purpose because he knows it ruffles my little feathers. I like the name Neffie and I feel it suits me just fine. That’s what my folks call me and that’s what I’ll only answer to. I flat out refuse to answer to anything else. Massa Sanderson, my slave Massa, is the chile of an Italian mother from Sicily, Italy and an English bred father who hails from Bowling Green, Kentucky.’<br /><br />That is the flavor that exudes form this period piece that is told with a degree of honesty and simplicity that makes the reader identify with the plight of slaves in the nineteenth century – and in turn, to appreciate the current focus on racism that plagues our nation at present. There is considerable action and events that propel the story forward and make us grateful that there are more volumes to follow. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5378698837646549825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whit" href="/user/show/7504369-whit">Whit</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391750026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer331400540696140000">I reviewed a complimentary copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br/><br/>Let me just start by saying how stressed out I was while reading this book. All of my senses were alert to what kept happening to Neffie and the situations she found herself in. I don’t know if I want to be proud of Neffie for not holding back exactly how she felt and fighting (mentally and physically) throughout the entire novel OR if I should be angry at how silly she was in a few of her altercations. <br/><br/>Ms. Blanche and</span>
  <span id="freeText331400540696140000" style="display:none">I reviewed a complimentary copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br /><br />Let me just start by saying how stressed out I was while reading this book. All of my senses were alert to what kept happening to Neffie and the situations she found herself in. I don’t know if I want to be proud of Neffie for not holding back exactly how she felt and fighting (mentally and physically) throughout the entire novel OR if I should be angry at how silly she was in a few of her altercations. <br /><br />Ms. Blanche and Mr. Colin ended up being her guardian angels, because the Massa in the story fought tooth and nail to knock her down a notch. The vivid descriptions allowed me to SEE the hate he felt for this young girl <br /><br />Ultimately, I loved everything about this book. The writing, the characters, and the drama. I will say the ending frustrated me a bit. I know it had to be a cliff hanger since it’s the first book of a series, but it felt like another story was starting up and then BOOM the end. <br /><br />To conclude my review, I’ll just say that I can’t wait for book 2 and to see how Neffie continues to grow. Great writing!</span>

<div id="review_2337993543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2337993543" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2337993543?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mar" href="/user/show/44401554-mar">Mar</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2337993543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15052765342623528482">The Chronicles of Neffie is one of those books that will touch your heart. The story will stay with you every time you close the book, not leaving your mind. And it doesn’t leave once it’s over. <br/>A.L Gibson wrote a beautiful and touching story about a fifteen-year-old girl. A black girl in the heart of Alabama in 1837. We are the witnesses of her life and struggles as a slave. We are taken through her own journey of understanding why she is in that situation, why the world treats her like she’s a</span>
  <span id="freeText15052765342623528482" style="display:none">The Chronicles of Neffie is one of those books that will touch your heart. The story will stay with you every time you close the book, not leaving your mind. And it doesn’t leave once it’s over. <br />A.L Gibson wrote a beautiful and touching story about a fifteen-year-old girl. A black girl in the heart of Alabama in 1837. We are the witnesses of her life and struggles as a slave. We are taken through her own journey of understanding why she is in that situation, why the world treats her like she’s an animal simply because of her skin color. The book is splendid, with marvelous descriptions and being narrated through Neffie’s point of view it only makes it more personal and hard. The author does a great job introducing the story and the characters and getting us involved in those tragic events. I can’t wait to read the rest of the series and find out more about what will happen.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2568619999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568619999" />
    <a title="Barbara Finazzo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74490515-barbara-finazzo"><img alt="Barbara Finazzo" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10922444978436919970"><strong>Good Beginning</strong><br/><br/>This started out interesting and was developing into what I thought would be a decent story. Neffie told of life as a slave and of her hopes for the future. Then the entire story shifted to her having to avoid her master as she was a "budding" girl. One thing I found very annoying was the fact that Neffie repe</span>
  <span id="freeText10922444978436919970" style="display:none"><strong>Good Beginning</strong><br /><br />This started out interesting and was developing into what I thought would be a decent story. Neffie told of life as a slave and of her hopes for the future. Then the entire story shifted to her having to avoid her master as she was a "budding" girl. The dialogue became very repetitive and nothing new was happening. This could have ended at about 60%. The end was very lacking as well. All in all this was a major let down. One thing I found very annoying was the fact that Neffie repeatedly told of her being able to read and write, but it was never told who or why she was taught. I would have thought that more background would have been given into what was repeatedly mentioned throughout the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10922444978436919970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16544614275279132660"><strong>Pre civil war short story</strong><br/><br/>This was a really great book on slavery before the civil war told almost in journal form from a young teenage girls view. It tells how slaves were just as smart as their masters, if not smarter, except they had to play the part of ignorant and dumb, so as to not get punished or sold. The start of what I hope is a great series.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cJ9iuNWtnlXqJ6tdeFM7QERgJ+iOWRDzjgwA51thCYzB7r0O3dWBLzQaAvE11iJIsiG7VUaiDDla9srGgVsaww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C63TimrF+dCaHldodiLqcPT0TfgMCIvEMAT1kTf14vu63Aw8Yr3mqkQj/sQ7p/N4ArXRRcTzlw7k/j+w7c/xtA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16123584877053938351">A.L. Gibson is a short story author, novelist, blogger and poet. Her first novel series, The Chronicles of Neffie, received a top review from Midwest Book Review and a five star rating from Readers' Favorite. When she is not writing or blogging, you can find her on the nearest bike trail. Feel free to connect with A.L. on her blog at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookinganita.com'>www.bookinganita.com</a>.</span>
